###begin article-title 0
###xml 34 58 34 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium yoelii yoelii</italic>
###xml 34 58 <span type="species:ncbi:73239">Plasmodium yoelii yoelii</span>
Assessment and improvement of the Plasmodium yoelii yoelii genome annotation through comparative analysis
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 0 11 0 11 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Motivation:</bold>
###xml 34 51 34 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium yoelii</italic>
###xml 302 311 302 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in silico</italic>
###xml 34 51 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">Plasmodium yoelii</span>
Motivation: The sequencing of the Plasmodium yoelii genome, a model rodent malaria parasite, has greatly facilitated research for the development of new drug and vaccine candidates against malaria. Unfortunately, only preliminary gene models were annotated on the partially sequenced genome, mostly by in silico gene prediction, and there has been no major improvement of the annotation since 2002.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 0 8 0 8 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Results:</bold>
###xml 554 563 554 563 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 604 617 604 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 752 761 752 761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 984 993 984 993 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 554 563 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 604 617 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 752 761 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 984 993 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1025 1030 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Results: Here we report on a systematic assessment of the accuracy of the genome annotation based on a detailed analysis of a comprehensive set of cDNA sequences and proteomics data. We found that the coverage of the current annotation tends to be biased toward genes expressed in the blood stages of the parasite life cycle. Based on our proteomic analysis, we estimate that about 15% of the liver stage proteome data we have generated is absent from the current annotation. Through comparative analysis we identified and manually curated a further 510 P. yoelii genes which have clear orthologs in the P. falciparum genome, but were not present or incorrectly annotated in the current annotation. This study suggests that improvements of the current P. yoelii genome annotation should focus on genes expressed in stages other than blood stages. Comparative analysis will be critically helpful for this re-annotation. The addition of newly annotated genes will facilitate the use of P. yoelii as a model system for studying human malaria.
###end p 2
###begin p 3
###xml 0 8 0 8 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Contact:</bold>

###end p 3

###end p 4
###begin title 5
1 INTRODUCTION
###end title 5
###begin p 6
###xml 168 178 168 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 195 201 195 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 203 207 203 207 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">2005</xref>
###xml 210 220 210 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
Malaria, a disease that causes more than 500 million clinical cases each year and kills more than 1 million worldwide in developing countries, is caused by unicellular Plasmodium parasites (Snow et al., 2005). Plasmodium is an obligatory intracellular parasite and its progression through the life cycle involves invasion of and intracellular replication in different tissues of both the mosquito vector and the mammalian host. Within the mammalian host, mousquito-inoculated salivary gland sporozoites of the parasite invade the liver and undergo an intracellular replication phase (schizogony) to produce merozoite stages that are competent for red blood cell infection. This initial blood stage infection establishes the blood stage cycle responsible for the pathology of malaria.
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 19 32 19 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 68 74 68 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 76 80 76 80 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">2002</xref>
###xml 97 114 97 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium yoelii</italic>
###xml 241 247 241 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 249 253 249 253 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">2002</xref>
###xml 378 391 378 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 429 435 429 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 437 441 437 441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">2005</xref>
###xml 458 462 458 462 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">2006</xref>
###xml 465 474 465 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 603 612 603 612 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 734 738 734 738 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">2003</xref>
###xml 789 799 789 799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. berghei</italic>
###xml 939 945 939 945 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 947 951 947 951 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">2006</xref>
###xml 19 32 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 97 114 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">Plasmodium yoelii</span>
###xml 363 368 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 378 391 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 465 474 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 603 612 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 647 652 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 701 706 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 789 799 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 878 884 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
Facilitated by the P. falciparum genome sequencing project (Gardner et al., 2002), the genome of Plasmodium yoelii was sequenced to 5-fold genome coverage using the whole-genome shotgun sequencing approach and was annotated in 2002 (Carlton et al., 2002). Comparative genome analysis has revealed high gene sequence similarities and genome-wide synteny among the human parasite P. falciparum and the rodent malaria models (Kooij et al., 2005; Roy and Hartl, 2006). P. yoelii is an important animal model for studying malaria biology, particularly of the liver stages and host-parasite interactions. The P. yoelii pre-erythrocytic infection of the mouse represents an accepted model closely reflecting human malaria (Luke and Hoffman, 2003). It is also a better model than the rodent model P. berghei for studying the elusive liver stages because it induces less inflammation in murine livers and produces more liver stage parasites (Tarun et al., 2006).
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 161 167 161 167 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 169 173 169 173 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">2008</xref>
###xml 202 211 202 211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 254 263 254 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in silico</italic>
###xml 406 415 406 415 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 432 438 432 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 440 444 440 444 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">2004</xref>
###xml 703 709 703 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 711 715 711 715 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">2006</xref>
###xml 880 893 868 881 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 939 945 927 933 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 947 951 935 939 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">2007</xref>
###xml 964 973 952 961 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 1175 1188 1163 1176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 1207 1211 1195 1199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">2007</xref>
###xml 1320 1326 1308 1314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1328 1332 1316 1320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">2006</xref>
###xml 1393 1402 1381 1390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 202 211 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 406 415 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 880 893 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 964 973 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1175 1188 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1393 1402 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
The partial genome sequencing approach has enabled the development of genome-wide approaches such as microarrays and proteomics to study parasite biology (Tarun et al., 2008). However, the genes in the P. yoelii genome database were mostly identified by in silico gene prediction and there is an inherent propensity for error using this methodology, especially when the genome is AT rich. For example, the P. yoelii S4 gene (Kaiser et al., 2004) is not included in the current annotation. Instead, a three-exon gene (PY00180 in PlasmoDB, ) is annotated on the opposite strand in the same genomic location. Later, S4 was reported to mediate parasite infection in its mosquito and vertebrate hosts (Kariu et al., 2006), clearly demonstrating the importance of this un-annotated gene in parasite lifecycle progression. A recent study estimated that approximately24% of the annotated P. falciparum genes contain errors of varying severity (Lu et al., 2007). Since the P. yoelii genome was partially sequenced and therefore not fully assembled, the error rate in the gene annotation is likely to be even higher when compared to the annotation of the fully sequenced and assembled P. falciparum genome (Salzberg, 2007). As an example of this error rate, the intensely studied gene encoding the circumsporozoite protein (Kumar et al., 2006) has been incorrectly annotated as two partial genes in the P. yoelii genome annotation (PY07368 and PY03168 in PlasmoDB).
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 33 42 33 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 161 170 161 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 212 222 212 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 257 263 257 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 265 269 265 269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">2005</xref>
###xml 316 326 316 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 457 466 457 466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 633 642 633 642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 790 800 790 800 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 863 872 863 872 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 908 921 908 921 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 1098 1108 1098 1108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 33 42 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 161 170 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 457 466 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 633 642 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 863 872 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 908 921 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1092 1097 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
The inaccurate annotation of the P. yoelii genome greatly compromises genome-wide studies. Thus, there is clearly a need for an updated and accurately annotated P. yoelii genome sequence. Fortunately, additional Plasmodium species have been sequenced (Hall et al., 2005), or are being sequenced (). Furthermore, the Plasmodium cDNA sequences available in Genbank have also grown dramatically since 2002. These provide an opportunity to examine the existing P. yoelii genome annotation using comparative analysis, to improve the current annotation and to discover missed genes. Here we describe a systematic assessment of the current P. yoelii annotation based on the publicly available cDNA sequence data and locally generated proteomic data. Based on the comparative analysis of published Plasmodium genome sequences, we have identified and manually curated 510 P. yoelii genes that have clear orthologs in P. falciparum, but are absent or incorrectly annotated in the current database. The improved annotation will greatly facilitate the use of the rodent malaria system in the modeling of human Plasmodium biology.
###end p 9
###begin title 10
2 METHODS
###end title 10
###begin title 11
2.1 cDNA sequence trimming and assembly
###end title 11
###begin p 12
###xml 4 14 4 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 395 405 395 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 743 749 743 749 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 751 755 751 755 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">2003</xref>
All Plasmodium expressed sequence tag (EST) sequences were downloaded from Genbank (August 2, 2007). To identify segments of EST sequences of vector origin, EST sequences were blasted against NCBI's UniVec Database using similar parameters as VecScreen (). Segments of vector origin were trimmed and only sequences with at least 100 bp were used. Trimmed EST sequences were then blasted against Plasmodium ribosomal gene sequences. Possible ribosomal RNA sequences were identified (with a match to a ribosomal gene of 40 bp or longer with a minimum of 90% identity) and removed. The ESTs of possible host origin were similarly identified and removed. The remaining EST sequences were clustered and assembled using TGI clustering tools (Pertea et al., 2003). Consensus sequences (contigs) were built based on two or more EST sequences that overlap for at least 40 bases with at least 94% sequence identity. These strict criteria helped to minimize the creation of chimeric contigs.
###end p 12
###begin title 13
2.2 Proteomics analysis
###end title 13
###begin p 14
###xml 51 57 51 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 59 63 59 63 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">2008</xref>
###xml 143 152 143 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 143 152 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 169 173 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Proteomics data were generated as described (Tarun et al., 2008). In brief, liver stage-infected hepatocytes were isolated from GFP-expressing P. yoelii-infected BALB/c mice by fluorescence-activated cell sorting. Total protein was extracted from sorted liver stage-infected hepatocytes and separated by polyacrylamide gel electrophoresis. Proteins were cut from the gel and digested in-gel with sequencing grade-modified trypsin. Mass spectra were obtained by nano-flow liquid chromatography tandem mass spectrometry (nano LC-MS/MS).
###end p 14
###begin p 15
###xml 59 68 59 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 195 204 195 204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 252 264 252 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mus musculus</italic>
###xml 332 342 332 342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. berghei</italic>
###xml 402 412 402 412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M.musculus</italic>
###xml 436 446 436 446 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M.musculus</italic>
###xml 672 681 672 681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 834 843 834 843 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 1537 1543 1537 1543 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1545 1549 1545 1549 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">2000</xref>
###xml 1727 1737 1727 1737 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M.musculus</italic>
###xml 59 68 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 195 204 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 252 264 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mus musculus</span>
###xml 332 342 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 402 412 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">M.musculus</span>
###xml 436 446 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">M.musculus</span>
###xml 672 681 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 834 843 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1532 1536 <span type="species:ncbi:4530">Rice</span>
###xml 1727 1737 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">M.musculus</span>
In an attempt to account for missing, partial or erroneous P. yoelii gene models, we assembled two additional databases besides a standard sequence database that combined the currently annotated P. yoelii protein sequences with the currently annotated Mus musculus protein sequences. The first database was assembled with annotated P. berghei protein sequences (PlasmoDB version 5.2) supplemented with M.musculus protein sequences. The M.musculus genome database was downloaded from the NCBI FTP site () on May 4, 2006. We constructed a second database to search for additional peptides that might not be found using current annotations. To do this, we translated all the P. yoelii genomic sequences downloaded from Genbank in all six frames and extracted all stop-to-stop open reading frames (ORFs). We used this approach since many P. yoelii genes have multiple exons and thus, not all peptides will be identified by searching a straightforward six-frame translation for contiguous sequences that contain start and stop codons. For instance, those peptides spanning exon boundaries will be missed with a standard six-frame ORF search, but they are critical for confirming and annotating splicing. To overcome the limitations of this straight-forward search, we also translated both the contigs and singlets derived from the EST analysis as described above in all six frames and again extracted all stop-to-stop ORFs and added these peptides to the second database. The six-frame translation was achieved using the EMBOSS package (Rice et al., 2000). All ORFs over 30 amino acids are merged. Redundant entries were removed using the WU-BLAST package [Gish W. (1996-2004) ]. This second sequence database was supplemented with M.musculus protein sequences as before.
###end p 15
###begin p 16
###xml 30 36 30 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 38 42 38 42 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">2008</xref>
###xml 214 220 214 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 222 226 222 226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">1994</xref>
###xml 304 310 304 310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 312 316 312 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">2002</xref>
###xml 904 905 904 905 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 950 960 950 960 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 1208 1217 1208 1217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 1314 1320 1314 1320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1322 1326 1322 1326 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">2000</xref>
###xml 1208 1217 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1309 1313 <span type="species:ncbi:4530">Rice</span>
The nano LC-MS/MS data (Tarun et al., 2008) were searched against each of the three sequence databases separately using BioworksBrowser 3.1 SR1 (San Jose, CA, ThermoElectron), which uses the SEQUEST algorithm (Eng et al., 1994). The search results were validated using PeptideProphet version 3.0 (Keller et al., 2002) for peptide identification. The PeptideProphet program scores the assignment of a particular MS spectrum to a known peptide. We considered only those PeptideProphet scores with a minimum P-value of 0.85, which in this case corresponds to a probability >98% of the peptide being correct. Depending on the database used for the analysis, single MS spectra could be assigned to different peptides. We kept only those spectra to which all peptides assigned were similar (in this case, they had no more than two amino acid differences between them). A total of 12 276 spectra with a minimum P-value of 0.85 were successfully assigned to Plasmodium protein sequences and 585 of the 12276 were assigned with two or more different peptides. Where common peptides differed slightly, a single representative peptide for each spectrum was chosen. Identified peptides were then mapped to the annotated P. yoelii protein sequences, genomic DNA sequences and EST sequences using tools provided by EMBOSS (Rice et al., 2000).
###end p 16
###begin title 17
2.3 Orthology mapping
###end title 17
###begin p 18
###xml 12 21 12 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 182 192 182 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 202 215 202 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 217 226 217 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 228 238 228 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. berghei</italic>
###xml 243 254 243 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. chabaudi</italic>
###xml 343 353 343 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 677 678 677 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 688 689 688 689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e</italic>
###xml 12 21 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 202 215 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 217 226 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 228 238 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 243 254 <span type="species:ncbi:99780|species:ncbi:5825">P. chabaudi</span>
To identify P. yoelii genes that were not included in the original annotation or incorrectly annotated, we created a database of homologous proteins, which mapped proteins from four Plasmodium species (P. falciparum, P. yoelii, P. berghei and P. chabaudi) into one-to-one orthologous relationships. The annotated protein sequences of the four Plasmodium species were downloaded from PlasmoDB version 5.2. All pair-wise comparisons among protein sequences from any two of the four genomes were performed using NCBI BLAST. For each protein, the best hit in each of the other genomes was detected. Orthologous proteins from two genomes were defined as reciprocal best hits (BLAST E-value < 1e-15 as cutoff).
###end p 18
###begin title 19
2.4 Protein features
###end title 19
###begin p 20
###xml 70 76 70 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 78 82 78 82 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">2004</xref>
###xml 204 210 204 210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 212 216 212 216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">2001</xref>
###xml 331 337 331 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 339 343 339 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">2007</xref>
Signal peptides were predicted using the SignalP 3.0 Server (Bendtsen et al., 2004) and only ORFs with a start codon were considered. Transmembrane domains were predicted using TMHMM Server v. 2.0 (Krogh et al., 2001). For Pfam domain annotations, protein sequences were searched against the Interpro database Release 15.0 (Mulder et al., 2007) using InterProScan web service.
###end p 20
###begin title 21
2.5 PCR verification of newly annotated genes
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 102 111 102 111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 715 722 714 721 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T5">Table 5</xref>
###xml 854 855 852 853 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#9675;</sup>
###xml 883 884 881 882 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#9675;</sup>
###xml 898 899 896 897 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#9675;</sup>
###xml 916 917 914 915 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#9675;</sup>
###xml 951 952 949 950 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#9675;</sup>
###xml 83 87 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 102 111 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
Genomic and total RNA were prepared from mixed blood stage parasites obtained from mice infected with P. yoelii at 3-5% parasitemia. Genomic DNA was extracted using the DNeasy kit (Valencia, CA, Qiagen) while total RNA was extracted using Trizol (Carlsbad, CA, Invitrogen) according to manufacturer's instructions. Total RNA was treated with Turbo-free RNAse-free DNAse (Austin, TX, Ambion) to remove contaminating genomic DNA in the preparation. First-strand cDNA was synthesized from 500 ng of total RNA using the Superscript III Platinum RT kit (Invitrogen). For each 25 mul PCR reaction, genomic DNA (25 ng) or cDNA (from 5 ng of total RNA) was used as template with 25 pmol of the forward and reverse primers (Table 5) and 12.5 mul of the Bioline Red PCR mix (Randolph, MA, Bioline) using the following cycling conditions: initial denaturation at 95oC for 3 min; 30 cycles of 94oC for 30 s, 55oC for 45 s and 72oC for 1 min; final extension of 72oC for 7 min.
###end p 22

###xml 228 237 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 913 922 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
EST sequences have been shown to be a powerful aid in Plasmodium gene identification and genome annotation (Carlton et al., 2002; Gardner et al., 2002; Hall et al., 2005; Li et al., 2003). Since the publication of the annotated P. yoelii genome in 2002 (Carlton et al., 2002), the number of Plasmodium cDNA sequences has increased dramatically (Table 1). In October 2002, there were 39 848 Plasmodium ESTs in Genbank. By August 2007, this number had increased by approximately350% to 138 827. Of note, is the generation of liver stage EST libraries (Ishino et al., GenBank accession DC195411-DC201252; Sacci et al., 2005; Wang et al., 2004). The liver stage has historically been extremely difficult to study (Blair and Carucci, 2005), but new tools have enabled isolation of rodent liver stages for analysis. The enrichment of Plasmodium cDNA sequences from all life stages has allowed us to examine the current P. yoelii annotation in far greater detail than previously possible. Table 1.Summary of the enrichment and pre-processing of Plasmodium EST data from GenbankOrganism10/20028/2007CleanedContigs (No. of ESTs)SingletsTotalYear of CoveragePublicationNo. of full-length genesAll four Plasmodium39 848138 827121 30815 605 (93 558)27 75043 355P. yoelii15 56218 93218 3192401 (12 293)6026842720025x5878P. berghei554458 95543 6655379 (32 528)11 13716 51620054x5864P. falciparum18 74238 70237 9595118 (30 875)708412 202200214.5x5268P.vivax022 23821 3652707 (17 862)3503621020054x5698
###end p 25
###begin p 26
###xml 48 58 48 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
Summary of the enrichment and pre-processing of Plasmodium EST data from Genbank
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 28 38 28 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 133 140 133 140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 200 209 200 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 281 282 281 282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 291 292 291 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e</italic>
###xml 200 209 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
We downloaded all available Plasmodium ESTs from Genbank, cleaned them, and then assembled them into large contigs after clustering (Table 1). We then mapped the contigs and singlets onto the current P. yoelii genome annotation by sequence similarity analysis using NCBI BLAST (an E-value <1e-15 cutoff was used).
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 55 62 55 62 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 451 458 451 458 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 785 792 785 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">similar</italic>
###xml 907 914 907 914 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 999 1007 999 1007 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Table 2.</label>
###xml 1096 1105 1096 1105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>

###xml 1096 1105 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
We classified the annotated genes into two categories (Table 2). A gene was considered as 'complete' if its annotated coding sequence (CDS) contained a start and stop codon. Otherwise the gene was considered 'partial'. Having EST evidence suggests that the annotated gene is very likely to encode a transcript. However, the exact boundaries of the gene cannot be verified explicitly unless an EST or EST contig contains a full length CDS. As shown in Table 2, longer gene sequences were better supported by an EST. It is possible that longer annotated genes were more likely to have representative ESTs. It is also possible that smaller genes were more likely to be incorrectly annotated, since short CDSs are more challenging for accurate computational prediction. When genes were of similar sizes, the gene was more likely to have a representative EST if its annotation was complete, rather than partial (Table 2). This implies that complete gene models are more likely to be correctly annotated. ###end p 28

###xml 48 57 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 107 116 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 387 396 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 751 760 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 779 788 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1159 1168 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
We found that there were significant numbers of P. yoelii ESTs that were not mapped to currently annotated P. yoelii CDSs (Table 3). Some un-mapped ESTs are likely to correspond to the untranslated regions of genes (both 5' and 3'), since only CDSs were used in the analysis. Interestingly there were relatively more ESTs from liver stage libraries that were not mapped to any annotated P. yoelii CDSs compared to those ESTs from blood stages (Table 3). About 50% of the liver stage EST sequences were not mapped, while only about 13% of blood stage EST sequences were not mapped. This suggests that the current annotation has a better coverage of transcripts expressed in blood stages than those expressed in liver stages. Table 3.Summary of mapping P. yoelii ESTs to annotated P. yoelii CDSscDNA libraryTotalCleanedMappedUnmapped (%)Asexual blood stages12 47112 04310 4741569 (13)Salivary gland sporozoite3091307220051067 (34.7)Axenic early liver stages (<24 h; trophozoite)14521387681706 (50.9)Liver stage (40 h; schizont)19161815845970 (53.4)Highlighted in bold are the percentage of ESTs from liver stage libraries which were not mapped to any annotated P. yoelii CDSs.
###end p 30

###begin title 33
###xml 22 31 22 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 22 31 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
3.2 Assessment of the P. yoelii genome annotation by proteomic analysis
###end title 33
###begin p 34
###xml 147 156 147 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 177 183 177 183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 185 189 185 189 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">2008</xref>
###xml 292 301 292 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 306 316 306 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. berghei</italic>
###xml 332 338 332 338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 340 344 340 344 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">2005</xref>
###xml 388 397 388 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 495 505 495 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. berghei</italic>
###xml 147 156 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 292 301 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 306 316 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 388 397 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 495 505 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
To further investigate the impact of current annotations on the studies of liver stage parasites, we used proteome data we generated from purified P. yoelii liver stages (Tarun et al., 2008). Since there is a high level of sequence similarity (91.3% identity at nucleotide level) between the P. yoelii and P. berghei genomes (Kooij et al., 2005), we hypothesized that a number of missing P. yoelii protein annotations would also be found by searching the annotated genome of the closely related P. berghei.
###end p 34
###begin p 35

###xml 68 78 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 171 176 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 266 275 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 338 348 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 400 409 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 536 545 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 591 601 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 683 692 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 800 809 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1272 1281 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1474 1484 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 1864 1873 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 2093 2102 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 2175 2184 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 2188 2198 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 2890 2899 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 3027 3036 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 3187 3196 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 3258 3267 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 3351 3361 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 3389 3398 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 3425 3434 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 3496 3505 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 3556 3565 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 3613 3623 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
We prepared a protein sequence database that included the annotated P. berghei protein sequences from the 4x coverage genome sequences (Hall et al., 2005) and the updated mouse protein sequences from NCBI. We then searched the spectra generated from our liver stage P. yoelii samples against this combined database. In total, 2644 unique P. berghei peptides were identified that had matches with our P. yoelii liver stage proteome data (Table 4 and Fig. 1). Only 87 (3.3%) of the peptides could not be perfectly mapped to any available P. yoelii sequence, suggesting that database searching P. berghei sequences or sequences from related Plasmodium species will supplement available P. yoelii annotations. Of the 2644 peptides, 2308 (87%), 2331 (88%) and 1666 (63%) peptides were perfectly mapped to P. yoelii annotated CDSs (PyCDS), genomic DNA (PyGdna) and EST (PyEST) sequences, respectively (Table 4). A total of 2249 peptides perfectly mapped to Plasmodium ESTs (Table 4, PlasEST) and of those, 952 matched to ESTs from three liver stage libraries (Table 4): PyLCM (Sacci et al., 2005), PyAxenic (Wang et al., 2004) and PbLS31 (Ishino et al. GenBank accession DC195411-DC201252). Of the 952 liver stage matched ESTs, 112 did not have a perfect match to any annotated P. yoelii proteins-about 12%. Similar estimations could be obtained when individual liver stage libraries were considered separately (9.6% for PyLCM, 11.5% for PyAxenic and 12.1% for PbLS31). Since the P. berghei genome sequence was only 4x coverage, we hypothesized that additional peptides were not identified by this analysis. The complete list of identified peptides is shown in . ###begin p 42
###xml 267 276 267 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 397 407 397 407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 267 276 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 472 477 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
To search for additional peptides that were not identified because of the limitations of the current annotations, we compiled a second protein sequence database. The second database contained: (1) all stop-to-stop ORFs over 30 amino acids after translating available P. yoelii genomic sequences from Genbank in six-frames, (2) stop-to-stop ORFs over 30 amino acids after translating pre-processed Plasmodium cDNA contigs and singlets in all six-frames and (3) the updated mouse protein sequences. The peptides were identified in the same way as above with this combined sequence database.
###end p 42

###xml 1322 1332 1322 1332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 1380 1389 1380 1389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 254 264 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 394 403 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 692 702 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 797 806 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 994 1003 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1056 1065 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1188 1198 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 1236 1245 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1380 1389 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
In total, 3512 unique peptides were identified (Table 4 and Fig. 1). Of these 3512 peptides, 2763 mapped perfectly to Plasmodium ESTs and 993 perfectly mapped to ESTs from liver stage libraries (PyLCM, PyAxenic and PbLS31). However, as was seen with the P. berghei database search, a certain percentage of peptides that matched to liver stage ESTs did not have a perfect match with the current P. yoelii protein annotation (15%, 148 of 993). As before, we obtained similar estimations when individual liver stage libraries were considered separately (16% for PyLCM, 15.1% for PyAxenic and 14.3% for PbLS31). Since the second sequence database was more comprehensive compared to the annotated P. berghei sequence database, and used sequences from the same species that the proteome data came from (P. yoelii), we consider this estimation to be closer to the actual situation. Thus, 15% of our liver stage proteome data that matches available liver stage EST data is not contained in the current P. yoelii annotation, suggesting that a significant number of P. yoelii genes/exons are not represented in the current annotation. There were 406 peptides were identified by searching annotated P. berghei protein sequences but not translated P. yoelii genome (Fig. 1B), showing that database searching of sequences from related Plasmodium species can supplement the partially sequenced P. yoelii genome. The complete list of identified peptides is shown in .

Pb: <italic>P. berghei</italic>. Pf: <italic>P. falciparum</italic>. Pc: <italic>P.chabaudi</italic>. Solid lines with two arrows indicate proteins from two corresponding species are reciprocal best blast hits. The number on the left indicates the number of orthologous groups in each category. The asterisk indicates the orthologous groups from which potential P<italic>. yoelii</italic> genes orthologous to <italic>P. falciparum</italic> genes were identified (also highlighted in bold).</p></caption>

###xml 69 78 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 186 196 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 201 211 <span type="species:ncbi:99780|species:ncbi:5825">P.chabaudi</span>
###xml 260 267 <span type="species:ncbi:5855">P.vivax</span>
###xml 272 282 <span type="species:ncbi:5850">P.knowlesi</span>
###xml 491 496 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 585 590 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 591 621 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">malaria parasite P. falciparum</span>
###xml 662 671 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 673 683 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 688 699 <span type="species:ncbi:99780|species:ncbi:5825">P. chabaudi</span>
###xml 828 841 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 894 907 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1082 1091 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1093 1103 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 1108 1121 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>

###xml 1221 1234 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1239 1249 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 1312 1325 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1330 1339 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1410 1423 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1428 1438 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 1505 1514 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1519 1529 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 1608 1621 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1626 1636 <span type="species:ncbi:99780|species:ncbi:5825">P.chabaudi</span>
###xml 1696 1705 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1936 1945 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1951 1961 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 1967 1980 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1986 1996 <span type="species:ncbi:99780|species:ncbi:5825">P.chabaudi</span>
###xml 2258 2267 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 2289 2302 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
To identify missing and incorrectly annotated genes in the annotated P. yoelii genome we took advantage of the recent genome publication of two closely related rodent Plasmodium species-P. berghei and P.chabaudi (Hall et al., 2005). Additional species such as P.vivax and P.knowlesi are also being sequenced. These additional sequences provide a great opportunity to improve current annotation by comparative analysis. Because rodent malaria parasites are used as model systems for studying human malaria parasites, we chose to focus on those genes that are well conserved between the human malaria parasite P. falciparum and the three rodent malaria parasites (P. yoelii, P. berghei and P. chabaudi) using the reciprocal best BLAST hit approach (Tatusov et al., 1997). First we identified a core set of genes conserved between P. falciparum and three rodent malaria parasites. Centered around P. falciparum proteins, we classified the mapping of orthologous proteins into six categories in the following order (Fig. 2): (1) those with three-way best BLAST hits among proteins from P. yoelii, P. berghei and P. falciparum (3285 proteins), (2) two-way best BLAST hits between proteins from P. falciparum and P. yoelii and P. falciparum and P. berghei only (271 proteins), (3) two-way best BLAST hits between only P. falciparum and P. yoelii (299 proteins) (4) two-way best BLAST hits between proteins from only P. falciparum and P. berghei (431 proteins), (5) two-way best BLAST hits between proteins from P. yoelii and P. berghei only (574 proteins) and (6) the two-way best BLAST hits between proteins from P. falciparum and P.chabaudi. Fig. 2.The strategy for the identification of orthologous P. yoelii genes potentially absent from the current annotation by comparative analysis. Orthologous genes from four Plasmodium species were identified based on the reciprocal best BLAST hit approach, and classified into six categories. Py: P. yoelii. Pb: P. berghei. Pf: P. falciparum. Pc: P.chabaudi. Solid lines with two arrows indicate proteins from two corresponding species are reciprocal best blast hits. The number on the left indicates the number of orthologous groups in each category. The asterisk indicates the orthologous groups from which potential P. yoelii genes orthologous to P. falciparum genes were identified (also highlighted in bold).
###end p 45

###begin p 47
###xml 40 53 40 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 76 86 76 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. berghei</italic>
###xml 94 104 94 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P.chabaudi</italic>
###xml 123 132 123 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 192 198 192 198 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Fig. 2</xref>
###xml 326 335 326 335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 533 546 533 546 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 577 590 577 590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 40 53 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 76 86 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 94 104 <span type="species:ncbi:99780|species:ncbi:5825">P.chabaudi</span>
###xml 123 132 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 326 335 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 533 546 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 577 590 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
The analysis enabled us to identify 530 P. falciparum genes which had clear P. berghei and/or P.chabaudi orthologs, but no P. yoelii orthologs based on the reciprocal best BLAST hit analysis (Fig. 2). This analysis provided strong evidence that those orthologous genes were absent from or incorrectly annotated in the current P. yoelii genome annotation, based on the assumption that the three rodent malaria parasite species are so closely related that genes are more conserved among the three than between any of the three and the P. falciparum genome. The list of candidate P. falciparum genes is provided in .
###end p 47
###begin p 48
###xml 30 43 30 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 126 135 126 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 201 210 201 210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 235 248 235 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 308 317 308 317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 543 549 543 549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 551 555 551 555 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">2007</xref>
###xml 675 681 675 681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 683 687 683 687 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">2005</xref>
###xml 694 700 694 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 702 706 702 706 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">2000</xref>
###xml 727 731 727 731 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">2005</xref>
###xml 30 43 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 126 135 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 201 210 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 235 248 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 308 317 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 689 693 <span type="species:ncbi:4530">Rice</span>
For each of the 530 candidate P. falciparum genes identified above, we attempted to manually annotate the orthologous gene in P. yoelii based on available genome sequences. First we searched candidate P. yoelii contigs by blasting the P. falciparum gene and its orthologs in other rodent species against the P. yoelii genomic sequences. Related EST sequences were also identified. The alignments were examined manually. For genes with multiple exons, we considered only those introns with the conserved eukaryotic intron splice site GT-AG (Lu et al., 2007). Publicly available software, databases and customized scripts were used to facilitate the manual annotation (Brejova et al., 2005; Rice et al., 2000; Slater and Birney, 2005). An internal MySQL database and the associated web interface were constructed to manage the data flow.
###end p 48

###xml 742 981 742 981 <table-wrap xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="T5" position="float"><label>Table 5.</label><caption><p textid="50">Summary characteristics of re-annotated orthologous <italic>P. yoelii</italic> genes</p></caption><table frame="hsides" rules="groups"><thead align="left"><tr><th align="left" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Category</th><th align="left" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Re-annotated genes</th></tr></thead><tbody align="left"><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">Total number</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">510</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">Span two or more Contigs</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">109</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">AAs (Mean, Min, Max)</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">310, 19, 4783</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">Transmembrane domain</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">116</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">Signal peptide</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">80</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">EST hit</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">452</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">Pfam domain</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">157</td></tr></tbody></table></table-wrap>
###xml 60 69 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 99 112 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 802 811 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
In total, we were able to manually annotate 510 orthologous P. yoelii genes from the 530 candidate P. falciparum genes (Table 5). About 90% (452/510) of these newly annotated genes had EST support, which is much higher than that of the existing annotated genes (Table 2). Interestingly, this new set of genes did not show the trend that larger genes tended to be better supported by EST evidence, as was seen in the existing annotated genes (Table 2). This implies that our manual curation is more accurate than the in silico prediction. About 21% (109/510) of the newly annotated genes spanned two or more contigs. The submission of newly annotated genes to public databases is in process. The current detailed annotations are provided in . Table 5.Summary characteristics of re-annotated orthologous P. yoelii genesCategoryRe-annotated genesTotal number510Span two or more Contigs109AAs (Mean, Min, Max)310, 19, 4783Transmembrane domain116Signal peptide80EST hit452Pfam domain157
###end p 49

###xml 160 169 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
We have verified the expression of seven of these re-annotated genes by PCR (Table 6 and Fig. 3). PCR amplification of cDNA prepared from mixed blood stages of P. yoelii confirms the presence of introns since the amplified products are smaller than the corresponding amplified DNA from genomic DNA. In six of the eight amplifications where introns are predicted, multiple bands in the resulting amplified cDNA were observed suggestive of alternative splicing. The gene for PY_PFB0505c, encoding beta-ketoacyl-acyl carrier protein synthase III, is predicted to be spanned by two separate contigs (Genbank ID 23485908 and 83285534) that encode the amino and carboxyl sequences of the protein. Although sequence information for the central portion of the gene is missing, using a forward primer from contig 23485908 and a reverse primer from contig 83285534, a approximately1.5 kb fragment is amplified from genomic DNA while multiple bands are observed from cDNA confirming that these two contigs are contiguous (1.PY_PFB0505c in Table 6 and Fig. 3). Fig. 3.PCR products confirming the expression of newly annotated genes. ###xml 1255 1259 1231 1235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">2007</xref>
###xml 1272 1281 1248 1257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 1514 1520 1490 1496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1522 1526 1498 1502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">2005</xref>
###xml 1617 1627 1593 1603 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 1652 1662 1628 1638 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 122 131 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 234 243 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 372 381 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1167 1180 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1272 1281 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
The accumulation of publicly available Plasmodium genomic and cDNA sequences enabled us to carefully examine the existing P. yoelii genomic annotations using comparative analysis. Our analysis confirmed that the incompleteness of the P. yoelii genome data has a considerable effect on the accuracy of the gene annotation (Salzberg, 2007). There were 5812 gaps left in the P. yoelii genome sequences when the sequencing project was finished (Carlton et al., 2002). Subsequent annotation was limited to approximately87% (20 of 23 Mb) of the genome. Therefore, many genes 'run-off' at the end of contigs. About 21% of the genes that we re-annotated were split across two or more contigs. Many partial genes, i.e. those genes without either an annotated start or stop codon, were predicted from these short fragments of DNA. Partial genes were less likely to be supported by EST sequences as shown in Table 2, and we feel that these predictions are less accurate than those for complete genes. Additional sequencing to close these gaps will greatly facilitate the improvement of the current annotation. In addition, it was recently estimated that approximately24% of the P. falciparum genes in the current database have been incorrectly predicted (Lu et al., 2007). Since the P. yoelii genes were predicted using similar bioinformatics software, we expect that improved gene finders may be able to generate more accurate gene models. For example, our limited experience with a gene finder known as ExonHunter (Brejova et al., 2005) indicates that similar methodologies using additional sources of information, especially Plasmodium EST sequences and other Plasmodium genome annotations, will greatly improve the prediction accuracy on the available sequences.
###end p 58
###begin p 59
###xml 212 221 212 221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 347 351 347 351 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2005</xref>
###xml 441 450 441 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 620 629 620 629 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 1044 1057 1044 1057 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 1107 1120 1107 1120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 212 221 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 441 450 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 620 629 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 1044 1057 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 1107 1120 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
Liver stages of the parasite life cycle are considered ideal targets for malaria vaccine and drug development. Our analysis indicates that the genes expressed in liver stages are under-represented in the current P. yoelii genome annotation compared to blood stages. This bias could further compromise the study of liver stages (Blair and Carucci, 2005). The likely reason for the bias is that many blood stage ESTs were generated before the P. yoelii genome was annotated and were subsequently incorporated into the genome annotation. However, liver stage EST sequences only became available after the annotation of the P. yoelii genome was completed. It is unlikely that genes expressed in liver stages are dramatically different to those expressed in other stages, thus a separate training dataset for gene finders will not be necessary to detect these genes in the genome. The availability of the liver stage ESTs, however, assist gene identification and the selection of correct gene models from alternative predictions. Since there are no P. falciparum liver stage EST sequences, it is likely that the P. falciparum genome annotation is also lacking in liver stage proteins. Therefore, annotating genes expressed in liver stages will benefit greatly from liver stage proteome and EST data from rodent malaria models.
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 256 266 244 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. berghei</italic>
###xml 490 499 478 487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 256 266 <span type="species:ncbi:5821">P. berghei</span>
###xml 490 499 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
Based on the proteomic analysis, we estimated the percentage of protein sequences that are not covered by current annotation to be 12approximately15%. Since the database from six-frame translations was more comprehensive compared to the one with annotated P. berghei protein sequences and used the sequences from the same species, we consider that the 15% is more realistic. Like the ESTs, the liver stage peptides presented here will provide a great resource for the future improvement of P. yoelii annotation and the identification of proteins expressed in the liver stages.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 69 78 69 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 145 155 145 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 335 344 335 344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 384 397 384 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 579 588 579 588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. yoelii</italic>
###xml 643 656 643 656 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. falciparum</italic>
###xml 69 78 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 335 344 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 384 397 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">P. falciparum</span>
###xml 579 588 <span type="species:ncbi:5861">P. yoelii</span>
###xml 620 625 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 626 656 <span type="species:ncbi:5833">malaria parasite P. falciparum</span>
We have provided here a systematic assessment of the accuracy of the P. yoelii genome annotation based on a detailed analysis of a comprehensive Plasmodium EST sequence database. The impact of the sub-optimal genome annotation on genome-wide experiments was evaluated using locally generated proteomics data. We identified a subset of P. yoelii genes that have clear orthologs in the P. falciparum genome but are absent from, or incorrectly annotated in current databases. These genes were manually annotated. This set of newly annotated genes will greatly facilitate the use of P. yoelii as a model system for studying human malaria parasite P. falciparum.
###end p 61
